INTRODUCTION
This report is a general analysis on the labor performed by the Section of
International Relations of the Directorio Revolucionario Estudiantil (TRES)
and en its plans for the future. However, it would take much time to make
a precise account on the labor accomplished in more than one year, so we
will limit it to be a general outline, hoping that in the near future a
more detailed one may be presented.
The TRES were not the most important.
The TRES firmly assert that the labor carried through by the Section of
International Relations has be-: a definite triumph for the organisation,
due to the importance of the ground of operation and the intensity with
which it has been developed. It is not an easy task to organise in such
a brief term an international field of operation like ours, which has
already born fruits and, in only one year, has attained great renom, even
outside the borders of our centiments. If all the motives for which the
IRS's Latin American Plan has attained such success were to be outlined,
we would never finish. We are going to list those which we consider are the
opinion.
A.- There can be no doubt that the most important labor has been the one
developed by the IRB Delegates in Latin America. During many months, the
economic support given to the Section of International Relations was so
short that only with the voluntary sacrifices of our delegates in Latin
America. The TRES was the only one of the most important labor groups
examples of generosity and self-sacrifice to our cause. There were
Delegates who, for many months, slept in costs and even on the floor,
others who lived sorroced by a wretched atmosphere, and others who
even want hungry. Our delegates fought to undergo all difficulties
and, many times against bealthie atmospheres, equipped only with their
enthusicians and their assert desire to carry our truth through America,
The series of our enterprise belong easily to the world.
B.- Inpatient the DRE identified with the struggles of Latin America. Services
with whom we have shared ideals and cooperation during this year.
C.- Inattaining the system of propaganda from Rianl to the labor which has
made the IRE known threepment the continent and has increased Deligations
its practice, in spite of the lack of information and economic means.
D.- Maintain the DRE inpatient of the United States, which has
been the most significant fighting for the retranscription of the
crossing out Battista's abhorrent past and Castro's inhuman present, and
holding an understanding posture towards the serious problems in Latin
America, social injustice, oppression, militarism and ignorance. We
have made also ours the lncing for the ransoming of our continent.
We have experienced all of the most important social issues. We
have been the most equally occasions, incomprehensions by those who we
had trusted. Monants of mechanertedness have lived within us more than
once, but our spirit has maintained its firmness still hoping that the

ORIGEN OF THE SECTION OF INTERNATIONAL RELATIONS
The Section of International Relations was created by the National Executive of
the IRS in the months of November-December 1960. Luis Boas Boedingues, of-Proxident
of the Faculty of Science of the University of Havana, was appointed for its
direction on January 1961, Mr. Eduardo Nuis was ordered to come to Miari and
was assigned the coordination of the DRE's labor in Latin America. Mr. Munis
arrived on the 8th of February, 1961.
THE FIRST STEPS
Before Munis's arrival at Miami, the DRE's activity in the international ground
was so limited that it lacked importance, even thought had sent a Delegation to
the Chancellars' assembly which was held on 1961 in the city of San Jose Costa,
the
Bureau of Economic Development, and the Department of Economic Development,
establishing contacts with student leaders in those countries. On the last days
of February 1961, a DRE Commission composed by Ernesto Fernandes Travioso, Tere-
sa Valdes Hurtado, and Eduardo Munis was sent to Washington for the purpose of
delivering a letter written by the DRE as genuine representation of Cuban Students
and the DRE's program. Mr. Richard Gudwin, the DRE's board of board members
to Mr. Richard Godwin (e ignore if it ever reached President Kennedy) It
stated the basis and ideals which moved the DRE the flight the Castro regime and
the common inspirations which led it together with the rest of Latin American
Students tomada the achievement if social justice for the people of our
researchers.
Despite all this - and for motives which have not yet been given to us - during
February, March, and April 1961, we were entirely restrained in the development
of our labor because of the poor admittance given to our plan. Our labor was
also a major role in the production of the industrial industry. The DRE was
of files of contacts and organizations, and to the maintaining relations with

five months (they assisted almost only by their own means) and so its labor
was reduced to the least.

THE CHANCELORS. CONFERENCE
When the Chancellore! Conference was held inJanuary 1964, there was a plan
to turn public opinion in favor of taking energetic steps against the Castro
regime. For this purpose, the 25th of January was appointed as the day in
which a Lu Marcha del Sienicoll ( The Silicone March) was to be carried through in
the principal Latin American cities, to give support to the Conference and protest
of the American Society. The American Society was a member of the American
astonishing. In Bolivia more than 20,000 people took part in " La Marcha del Si-
lencio", they all carried lighted torches since it was a night fall. In Peru,
more than 10,000 persons were assembled and in daysquil, Becuador, around 5,000.
The 1970s, the American Society was a member of the American Society.
The IRs Delegation seen to the Chancellors Conferences visited several countries
before arriving at Montevideo, so as to develop in them the labor of propaganda
and organization previous to the events that would take place during the Confe-
nence of the American Society. The American Society was a member of the
by Juan M. Salvat, Fernando Garcia Chacon, Jose Maria Lasa, Ernesto Pernandes
Travieso, and Mario Pita. This group visited Bolivia, Peru, Chile, and Argenti-
na. The second group was composed only by Eduardo Munis, who visited Honduras,
and the American Society. The American Society was a member of the American
vices with secretaries of Foreign Relations, and with Presidents of the nations,
were hold. In Uruguay, the first photograph exhibition was shown in the Plaza
Libertad, a gigantic meeting was held in Montevideo and four meetings were held
in other cities of the county (San Carlos, Pirizpolis, Minas, and Maldonado),
pest bounds were placed at the Communist meeting in the Univeral by, press com-
ferences were held, and radio programs were broadcasted, all during the Confer-
ence.

several countries of Africa (Genegal, Ghana, Kenya, Egypt, Marruecos, Nigeria,

Africa in preparation for the CIE.

DEPYCTENCIÉS AND DI PHTCULTIFS
During more than one year of vigorous working, the Section of International Rela-
tions has encountered countless deficiencies and difficulties, may of which have
been already surpassed, though others still prevail. He will state bellow the
main difficulties which we are actually facing and which we endeavor to surpass
as soon as possible.
1.- Personnel
The problem on lack of personnel has been and is one of the main difficulties
which the Section has encountered in its labor. Countless are the motives for
this, among which we can list.
A.- Lask of capable personnel I Due to the importance of the labor developed in
Latin America, the personnel with capacity for the work is not very abundant.
B.- Personal problems of the aspirants to Delegates I This is one of the most
conflictive motives we are actually flexible. The results are as follows:
1. The problem of the personnel has been as actually taking place is a
massive exodus of our people. Consequently, being in the need of working to
help their families, many Belogates have had to give up their labors and scope-
ration with us. In many cases, aspirants to Delegates have been forced to abandon
the Plan reauding only a few days for their departments.
C.- Problems on obtaining vises: The difficulties in obtaining the visas for several
countries (like Colombia, Mexico, KI Salvador, Santo Domingo ) has abso, on
the basis of the development of the personnel. It also believes for Latin America. There
is a specific example in Mexico, for which it has been absolutely impossible
to obtain the visas; in spite of all the efforts made, the deal of deblagates in these
said conditions of anactivity have consequently abandoned the system.
D.- Problems of Delegates in the respective countries: The problems the Delegates
have had to face in the different countries have been so many that it results
imposible to outline them all. We will try to point out fow those which we consi-
dor are the most importit;
a.- Economic difficulties : The Delegates lacked operational funds to develop
their plans for approximately one year. Their field of operation was
logically reduced to the least. Actually the delegates do have these funds,
though, evidently, many of the plans could not be carried through them.
b.- Problems with American officials in the different countries: Though in the
majority of the countries our relations are the best,nevertheless, we hate
bad to face problems in some. For example, in Honduras we have had to
be a very good way to do this. For example, of Rattista supporters. In our Delegation
at Sao Paolo, Brasil, our Delegates are the most important to clean Fields, Jussas
simple workers, ( they were not sent to Latin America for some purposes).
and further more they have even been prohibited to use the name of the ins.

SESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESESE
